Comfortable seating and a pleasant atmosphere make it fine for relaxing, just avoid ordering espresso drinks. Bo's Coffee - Rizal Boulevard, Dumaguete ★★★☆☆ 03 Jul 2019 Sol y Mar Building, Dumaguete, 6200 Negros Oriental, Philippines The cappuccino quality here varies wildly from day to day, but at least it can occasionally be decent. Make sure to request no cinnamon and insist on a proper mug instead of paper cups. Mediocre as it is, this still remains one of the very few tolerable coffee options in town. Cafe Racer Diner ★★★☆☆ 26 Jun 2019 EJ Blanco Drive, corner Flores Ave, Dumaguete, 6200 Negros Oriental, Philippines Funky retro-style diner next to Lantaw with fair prices and a relaxed atmosphere. Better suited for beers and casual drinks than for coffee, which is fairly poor. Food is acceptable but not especially memorable. Casablanca Restaurant Dumaguete - Cafe Bar & Fine Dining ★★★★★ 15 Apr 2022 Rizal Boulevard, Corner Noblefranca St, Dumaguete City, 6200 Negros Oriental, Philippines I have been frequenting Casablanca for more than a decade now and never had a bad meal. The Austrian owner is a proper restaurateur and knows his business. It's hard to find consistently good food in the provinces in the Philippines and Casablanca is a heaven sent. If this was in Bangkok or Singapore it wouldn't be a five star place, for sure, this is simple food, not some creative fine dining, but in the Visayas you won't find anything better than this. Casablanca is in a prime location on Rizal Blvd and on nice days you can enjoy the view over the deep blue ocean and Siquijor. Since traffic in Dumaguete is getting worse every year, however, the air conditioned dining room is a good alternative. Guenther, the proprietor, is also serious about wines, and he offers a decent collection of reasonably priced, good value wines to accompany his food. Casablanca serves very eclectic international fare, from seared tuna to hearty Central European meat platters. There's also a small menu of Filipino favourites, which are as good as any you can find in the region's local restaurants. Their lunch deals are incredible. 270 Php will buy you a soup, a salad, a beer and a generous main course. One of the reasons I'm writing this review is to express my complete incredulity about some reviewers here, who say this place is too expensive. It really isn't! It's actually incredibly good value for what you get. I'd even go as far as to say, for the same amount of meat they serve here, you'd pay more in some basic local carinderia, and the taste won't be half as good. The service tends to be pretty bad, that's true, especially when the owner is out of town, which can be quite frustrating to be honest. But that's the same everywhere in the country and the quality of the food that comes out of the kitchen has never disappointed. Casablanca is quite simply a must visit for everyone who likes wine and good food when in the Visayas. Flip Flops Restobar ★★★★☆ 03 Jul 2019 872X+8GW, Jose Romero Road, Dumaguete, Negros Oriental, Philippines Simple but excellent little restobar attracting a pleasant mix of locals and expats. The Filipino bar food is surprisingly good and they also serve proper wood-fired pizzas. The kinilaw and sisig are especially recommended. Not exactly cheap, but very good value overall and probably my favourite hangout in Dumaguete. Hayahay Treehouse Bar and Viewdeck‎ Restobar ★★★★☆ 02 Jul 2019 201 Flores Ave, Dumaguete, 6200 Negros Oriental, Philippines Still one of the best nights out in Dumaguete after all these years. Cheap drinks, decent food, live music and a reliably lively atmosphere. Usually packed on weekends for good reason. KRI Catering ★★★★☆ 02 Apr 2020 53 Silliman Ave, Dumaguete, 6200 Negros Oriental, Philippines Kri is Dumaguete's most ambitious restaurant. With an open kitchen and a stylish dining room (don't be put off by the simple front room) they're trying their hands at creative international cooking and some Filipino dishes with a twist. Not everything works and the service is friendly, but often a little incompetent. But for the most part, the food served here is some of the best in town and I've been coming here for almost a decade Allegre Bar ★★★★★ 20 Jun 2019 8845+QW8, Dumaguete, Negros Oriental, Philippines This tiny, yet elegant hole-in-the-wall is elevating the gastronomic options of Dumaguete to new standards, with their authentic tapas bar atmosphere, very good food and inexpensive cocktails. Stepping into Allegre feels like stepping into a little piece of Spain on what used to be the Philippines' most attractive seafront Boulevard. There's not much room inside but sitting at the bar is perfectly fine, sitting outside is a bit marred because traffic has become quite ridiculous here recently. The have a very small menu, but a great addition of daily specials which are the real winners of this place. Delicious ceviche, lovely chorizo, croquetas, and the star of all tapas dishes : morcilla, home made Spanish blood sausage, which really made me happy to see this rare dish (in Asia) on the menu. Prices are very reasonable, in line with Dumaguete's low level, with all dishes under 200 Php, and cocktails are tasty and downright cheap. Neva's Pizza ★★★★☆ 02 Jul 2019 Hibbard Ave. coner Amigo Subdv Bgy, Dumaguete, 6200 Negros Oriental, Philippines I already loved Neva's back in my backpacker days, when their wood-fired kuripot pizzas were probably among the cheapest on earth and still genuinely tasty. These days it remains excellent value and an easy recommendation for anyone travelling on a budget. Lantaw Native Restaurant ★★★★☆ 30 May 2021 EJ Blanco Drive, corner Flores Ave, Dumaguete City, 6200 Negros Oriental, Philippines Large menu of Filipino favourites served at very fair prices considering the quality and location. The squid sisig and tuna belly are particularly good, and even the halo-halo is nicely done. Probably the best place for Filipino food in Dumaguete. Pasta King Cafe di Roma ★★★☆☆ 02 Jul 2019 South Sea Road, Fatima Village, Dumaguete, Negros Oriental, Philippines Everything here is reasonably decent, from the pizza to the cakes and coffee, but nothing really stands out. The coffee may actually be among the better ones in Dumaguete, which admittedly is not saying much. Prices are fair, though the café itself is not especially comfortable for lingering. Sans Rival Cakes & Pastries ★★☆☆☆ 26 Jun 2019 165 San Jose St, Dumaguete, 6200 Negros Oriental, Philippines Nice boulevard location and the cakes are perfectly acceptable, but almost everything else is disappointing. The breakfasts, savoury food and coffees are all underwhelming. Best treated purely as a cake stop. Sans Rival Cakes & Pastries | Robinsons Dumaguete ★★☆☆☆ 26 Jun 2019 78X3+F69, Calindagan Rd, Dumaguete, Negros Oriental, Philippines I genuinely struggle to understand this place's popularity. The food is poor, the coffee worse, and this branch somehow manages to be even weaker than the original shop in town. The cakes are alright, but nowhere near good enough to justify the hype. Señorita's Mexican Grill, Dumaguete Airport ★★★☆☆ 02 Jul 2019 87JW+W74 Dumaguete–Sibulan Airport, Dumaguete, 6200 Negros Oriental, Philippines Prices are naturally higher than in town, but still reasonable for an airport restaurant. The food is decent enough and it's certainly a far more comfortable place to wait for a flight than the rather shabby airport lounge itself. Soban Korean Restaurant ★★★★☆ 20 Jun 2019 Sacred Heart, Real St, Dumaguete, Negros Oriental, Philippines Soban has been around for a long time and they're still going strong, in spite of their rather unfortunate location in a run down strip mall along the highway on the outskirts of town. In order to survive in such a location, you must be able to offer something special and unique. Soban offers authentic, traditional Korean food at reasonable prices, and makes the trip out well worth it. The prices for individual dishes might look steep by Dumaguete standards but you get a lot for your money, free appetisers, a pot of tea and ice tea, plus the portions are really big, so it's best to come in a group or be prepared to take half of your food back home. They're doing nice dumplings and seafood pancakes (a bargain at 200 Php, the price hasn't changed in years) but their killer dish is osom bulgogi, which should be called awesome bulgogi, really. It's expensive at 600 something pesos, but while they say it's good for 2, it actually feeds 4 easily. I'm generally not too impressed with their appetisers (dry pancake, slightly too sweet pickles) and the atmosphere is not terribly inviting, therefore it's only a four star place for me, but for lovers of Korean food, Soban is a must visit while in Dumaguete. Sta. Teresa Resto San Juan Branch ★★★☆☆ 03 Jul 2019 8855+Q58, Dumaguete, Negros Oriental, Philippines An upmarket carinderia serving some of the most authentically Filipino food in town, for better or worse depending on your palate. Many of the pre-cooked dishes are intensely rich, pungent and rather fatty, very much designed to be eaten with large amounts of rice.

PROV: Palawan / San Vicente · 16 reviews
NAME: Ayette's Bamboo Balai Balai
ADDR: 
TEXT: ★★★★☆ 24 Mar 2025 C56G+PRH, Risal St, San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines I stayed here way back in 2009 when Port Barton was still a quiet, off-the-beaten-path village. At that time, they had just built their first bungalow, which cost a fraction of today’s price. While the accommodation has gotten much more expensive, the restaurant is still a great place to eat. Food prices are similar to other spots in town—on the pricey side—but the quality is good. Plus, they serve the cheapest beer in Port Barton, which is obviously a bonus! The Beach Barn (Summer Homes) ★★★★☆ 24 Mar 2025 · ₱200–400 C57H+C5J The Beach, San Vicente, 5309 Palawan, Philippines This place is anything but stylish—the décor is pretty awful. But if you can look past that, it’s the cheapest spot for drinks and food right on the beach. Perfect for grabbing a few beers, enjoying the sunset, and having a quick snack without breaking the bank. Just don’t expect any aesthetic charm! Kape San Vicente ★★★★☆ 20 Mar 2025 Boulevard, Purok, Rosal, Barangay Poblacion, San Vicente, 5309 Palawan, Philippines Great to find something resembling a modern coffee shop with an espresso machine outside the main tourist centres. Prices are about half of what you'd pay in Port Barton, both for food and coffee. If you're a coffee purist, I'd probably avoid the milk-based drinks—the milk they use seems to be sweetened or flavoured. But for the price, it's well worth a stop on the way north. Kitzmon Food House ★★★★★ 24 Mar 2025 · ₱1–200 · Lunch J85G+5J, San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines This place is much neater and cleaner than your average provincial Foodhaus, offering a good variety of Filipino favorites, including Chaolong, the Palawan version of Vietnamese beef stew. The prices are very reasonable, and the service is friendly. It’s probably the best food option outside of the resorts for many miles. Definitely worth a visit! Master Chaolong ★★★★☆ 24 Mar 2025 · ₱1–200 · Dinner C55G+WM8, San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines Master Chao Lang has so much potential but doesn’t seem to care about attracting customers. It’s right next to Star Apple, Port Barton’s most popular (and overpriced) restaurant, yet it stays oddly low-profile. The food is actually good—big portions of tasty Vietnamese-Filipino beef noodles and banh mi-style sandwiches, perfect for budget travelers. But the uninterested staff, questionable cleanliness, and uninspiring decor make it feel like they’re actively trying to drive people away rather than welcome them. A shame, because with the right approach, this place could be a hit! Milano Café ★★★★☆ 18 Mar 2025 Quezon Street, San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines Very good Italian coffee in a modern, fan-cooled setting. The cappuccino is well prepared, though the milk quality isn’t the best—not really their fault, as even the “fresh” milk in Palawan has that distinct UHT aftertaste (something I’ve noticed more than once). Prices are on par with Europe or Manila, but then again, Port Barton is generally expensive. Prince John Resort ★★★★★ 19 Mar 2025 San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines We only stopped for drinks, but the setting is absolutely gorgeous, easily one of the most beautiful spots around Port Barton. It's tricky to reach and was almost empty when we visited, and yes, it's on the expensive side, but for a location like this the prices are totally justified. Well worth the ride out for a drink with a view. Amwani Sunset Colours Camping Site ★★★★★ 24 Mar 2025 Erawan Beach, San Vicente, 5302 Palawan, Philippines Since they paved the roads all the way up here from San Vicente, this place feels less remote than it must have been just a few months ago. The beach is stunning, and despite the waves, it’s probably the best beach I’ve found in Palawan for actual swimming, not just lounging, thanks to the steep entrance. The resort itself is quite basic but would be a great spot for a long-term stay. They have a shared kitchen for everyone to use, and they even sell beer at cost price. Their food prices are fair as well, as portions are big. Sadly, the two Seaview bungalows were fully booked during our visit. These would definitely be the best rooms to stay in, and I’d advise everyone to try and book one of those. Our family room was nice enough and spacious, and it even had its own small kitchen. However, it’s not right on the beach, so if you can, go for the Seaview bungalows for the best experience. Bato ni Ningning ★★★★★ 24 Mar 2025 M85H+5X5, Alimanguan National Hwy, San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines A beautifully manicured viewpoint offering some of the most stunning views on the island. Despite its remote location, it’s definitely worth the trip. Now that the road is fully paved, it’s not even a very hard journey to get here. A must-visit for breathtaking views! Bigaho falls ★★★★★ 24 Mar 2025 Philippines, Palawan, San Vicente, 5309 A lovely little waterfall tucked away in the jungle! The surroundings are beautiful, and the short walk to the falls is pleasant and well-maintained. The entrance fee (40 pesos) is totally fair since the locals provide nice amenities and keep the path in good condition. Getting here from Port Barton is still a bit tricky—the road is mostly unpaved, and I wouldn’t recommend using a scooter in the rainy season. The main pool under the waterfall can get crowded, but there are plenty of smaller pools downstream where you can relax in peace. Definitely worth a visit! Dheltor Hilltop ★★★★★ 24 Mar 2025 C55J+XGM, Port Barton - San Jose Rd, San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines Probably the best budget accommodation we’ve found in all of Palawan! The biggest highlight is the lovely little swimming pool—clean, well-maintained, and never crowded. The bungalows are neat, the shared bathrooms are spotless, and the included breakfast is surprisingly generous, with both Filipino and Western options. For the price, it’s a great deal, especially for Port Barton where accommodation tends to be overpriced. Highly recommended! Imuruan Viewpoint ★★★★☆ 21 Mar 2025 M88M+57, San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines Very pretty views over the coastline and the outlying islands. No entrance fee. Lumambong Beach ★★★★★ 24 Mar 2025 Philippines This beach is about as far up as you can go from San Vicente along this part of the coast. It’s very remote, and the last six or seven kilometers are quite rough, but it’s absolutely worth it if you're looking for a beautiful, unspoiled tropical beach. You can access it through Binga Beach Resort, or you can take the adventurous route by crossing a rickety wooden bridge over a small creek to get to the beach just past the resort. Chances are, you'll have the beach all to yourself. It’s also a great spot for swimming. Pamuayan Beach ★★★★★ 24 Mar 2025 C5MQ+538, San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines Just a short but bumpy ride from Port Barton, this beach is far less popular than White Beach. Yet, it’s stunningly picturesque—with the bankas and the sandbar, it looks like something straight out of a travel magazine. Sparkling Beach ★★★★★ 21 Mar 2025 San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines Very beautiful spot where the lagoon meets the sea. Easy public access to this beach. Still feels remote and waiting to be discovered although the roads leading here are now paved all the way from San Vicente White Beach ★★★★★ 24 Mar 2025 C543+6X8, San Vicente, Palawan, Philippines White Beach is absolutely stunning—one of the most beautiful in Palawan! The sand is soft, the water is crystal clear, and the atmosphere is super relaxed. However, getting here is a bit of an adventure. The road is rough, and after rain, it might be nearly impossible to pass. It's also quite popular, especially with backpackers, so don’t expect a secluded paradise. One downside: they charge a 50 Peso entrance fee but provide zero amenities—no toilets, no changing rooms, nothing. Not sure where that money goes. Still, the beach itself is 100% worth a visit!

PROV: Palawan / Taytay (near) · 2 reviews
NAME: LEONIDA'S
ADDR: 
TEXT: ★★★★★ 24 Mar 2025 · ₱200–400 · Lunch Taytay, Palawan, Philippines How unexpected to find such a beautiful garden café, seemingly in the middle of nowhere, somewhere in provincial Palawan. Leonidas is truly a gem. Not only is it beautifully decorated, but the service is also very friendly, and the food is on par with some of the better Filipino restaurants in the big cities. Their crispy pork kare-kare was absolutely mouth-wateringly delicious. Prices are very reasonable for this kind of food quality in such an environment. They even serve really good, proper coffees, though they’re a bit on the pricey side. Definitely a must-visit spot! Casa Rosa Seaview Inn & Restaurant ★★★★☆ 28 Mar 2025 Taytay, Palawan, Philippines A very quiet resort on a hill above Taytay, with beautiful views over the town and bay from the restaurant terrace. The service is slow and the food is so-so, but as a rest stop on the long ride between El Nido and Puerto Princesa it's a lovely place to pause. With more time, I'd happily have broken the trip here for a night.

MTR (KL Sentral) ★★★★☆ 13 Feb 2026 · RM 20–40 · Breakfast 69, Jalan Thambipillay, Brickfields, 50470 Kuala Lumpur, Wilayah Persekutuan Kuala Lumpur, Malaysia I had a very enjoyable meal at the original branch of MTR in Bangalore some time ago. Since I was staying around Kuala Lumpur Sentral and more or less stumbled across this place, I decided to give it a try. The biggest difference between the two locations is clearly the pricing — quite a bit higher here in Kuala Lumpur than in Bangalore. On the other hand, this branch comes recommended in the Michelin Guide, which generally suggests a certain level of reliability when it comes to food quality. Unfortunately, the mini thalis are only served from 11:30 onwards. Since I went there for breakfast, I ended up with vadas and idlis instead. Still, the basics are done properly, so it’s a good place for breakfast. Prices aren’t exactly cheap by local standards, but they remain acceptable overall. Air Terjun Taeno ★★★★☆ 15 Mar 2026 9569+X9H, Rumah Tiga, Teluk Ambon, Kota Ambon, Maluku, Indonesia Air Terjun Rumatiga is a very nice waterfall surprisingly close to Ambon city. You pay a small entrance fee of 5,000 rupiah and then follow a paved path with many steep stairs down to the falls. The walk is quite demanding, especially on the way back up, which probably keeps the crowds away. When I visited during the week there was nobody else there. The waterfall itself is beautiful and there is a natural pool at the bottom where you can cool off, although the rocks can be slippery and getting into the water requires a bit of care. The whole place is not particularly clean, but that unfortunately seems to be a general issue on Ambon. A worthwhile stop near the city and easily one of the nicest natural sights on the island. BIZ HOTEL CITY CENTER AMBON ★★★★☆ 15 Mar 2026 Jl. Maluku Said Perintah, Kel Ahusen, Kec. By local standards the hotel and the rooms are modern and clean. Air conditioning and Wi-Fi both worked well, and the bathroom was surprisingly good. The only real downside is the room size. The rooms are quite small. At 350K per night including breakfast, though, the hotel still offers good value for a short stay in Ambon, especially if you want to be central and close to the port. Rozongain Vitalia Guest House(Resort) ★★★★☆ 14 Mar 2026 Jalan tanjung Kenari No.Rt.01, Maluku 97593, Indonesia Vitalia Resort is one of the main places to stay on Pulau Hatta. When I arrived all the good bungalows were already taken, so I spent the first night in one of the overflow rooms in the main building. These rooms are very basic, with just a bed, a fan and a simple bucket bathroom. The next day I moved into one of the beach bungalows, which was clearly worth the wait. The bungalow itself was lovely, with very comfortable hammocks, a spacious terrace and a carefully designed interior that felt more like a private little holiday home than a typical homestay hut. The price was 450K per person including all meals. Food was very good by remote island standards. We were served freshly caught fish, often barracuda, twice a day, together with vegetables, salad and sometimes tempeh or aubergine, plus a simple coconut soup. The resort also sits on the best part of the beach, one of the few parts of the island that still has proper sand and does not disappear completely at high tide. If you get that one bungalow it's a great place to stay on Pulau Hatta. The aubergines and the ulang-ulang were fine, though fairly standard. The ayam bakar was disappointing. Instead of proper grilled chicken meat, I was served a couple of small wings completely drowned in sweet kecap manis. That was not what I expected when ordering grilled chicken. Prices are moderate and slightly lower than some other tourist-oriented places on the island. Service was friendly. Overall, Nusantara is a decent option when other places are closed, but the cooking was the least memorable of the meals I had in Banda Neira. SERENADE FOOD & BEVERAGE ★★★★★ 14 Mar 2026 · Rp 25–50k RT.02, Dwi Warna, Banda, Central Maluku Regency, Maluku 97593, Indonesia Serenade serves the best coffee I found in Banda Neira. The café clearly tries to bring a bit of modern coffee culture to the island and the machine espresso drinks are surprisingly decent. A latte costs 20K and the quality is better than expected for such a remote place. They also serve simple bistro dishes. We had spaghetti aglio e olio with prawns and ayam goreng with a spicy sambal, both well prepared and very inexpensive at around 20–25K. The main drawback is the opening hours. Serenade only opens at 5 p.m., which makes it impossible to get good coffee there in the morning. Spice Island Cafe ★★★★☆ 14 Mar 2026 · Rp 125–150k · Dinner Nusantara, Banda, Central Maluku Regency, Maluku, Indonesia Spice Island Café is probably the most popular place in Banda Neira with Western tourists. One reason is that it is reliably open throughout the day, which cannot be said for many other restaurants on the island. The menu covers a range of local dishes. I tried ulang-ulang with kenari nut sauce, sup pala (nutmeg soup), and fish aru-aru. The food was generally well prepared and portions were reasonable. Prices are somewhat higher than elsewhere on the island because the café adds a 10% tax to the bill, something no other restaurant in Banda Neira seems to do. It is a simple, but dependable place to eat and one of the few restaurants where you can usually get food even when many other places are closed. Airport Reef Snorkel Site ★★★★★ 15 Mar 2026 FWH5+XM, Kampung Baru, Central Maluku Regency, Maluku, Indonesia Airport Reef lies just off the eastern end of the airport runway on Banda Neira and is one of the most impressive snorkeling spots close to town. The reef here is in excellent condition, with dense soft and hard corals that look very healthy. For a site located so close to town, the quality of the reef is remarkable. Fish life is plentiful, though not quite as overwhelming as at some sites in Raja Ampat. I saw giant puffers, titan triggerfish and several reef sharks, and there was a constant stream of smaller reef fish along the coral slope. The reef continues for a surprisingly long stretch along the coast. I spent more than two hours snorkeling along it and still had not seen the entire area. A beautiful and very healthy reef and one of the best snorkeling spots around Banda Neira. Benteng Holandia ★★★★★ 15 Mar 2026 FV2J+RF2, Lonthor, Banda, Central Maluku Regency, Maluku, Indonesia Fort Hollandia is one of the main historical sights on Banda Besar. From the jetty it takes about 45 minutes to reach on foot by following the coastal road through several villages. The walk itself is very pleasant. The villages on Banda Besar are clean, colourful and well kept, and the whole way you have constant views across the water toward Banda Neira and the impressive Gunung Api volcano. The fort itself dates back to the 17th century. Only ruins remain today, but the hilltop location offers an outstanding view across the strait toward Banda Neira and the volcano. Worth visiting mainly for the walk and the views rather than the ruins themselves. Hatta Island ★★★★★ 14 Mar 2026 C29M+7Q8, Hatta Island, Central Maluku Regency, Maluku, Indonesia The best thing about staying on Pulau Hatta is the house reef. The reef starts roughly 50 metres from the beach, so you can reach excellent snorkeling without needing a boat. The coral itself is not quite as dense or healthy as around Banda Neira, but the main attraction here is the long drop-off that runs along the coast for more than a kilometre. Swimming along this wall you see a huge amount of fish life, including plenty of very large fish such as Napoleon wrasse. During almost every snorkelling session I saw turtles, usually a dozen or so, as well as several reef sharks of different sizes. On one occasion I also spotted a very large stingray, almost the size of a small manta. Visibility directly in front of the main beach can be quite poor. It improves significantly if you swim left from Vitalia or south from the pier toward Terapung, where visibility of around 20–25 metres is common, even in bad weather. Allan Bungalow ★★★★★ 14 Mar 2026 FVFR+RR8, gunung Api, Nusantara, Banda, Central Maluku Regency, Maluku, Indonesia I stayed at Allan’s on Banda Api for more than a week. The location is excellent, directly across the strait from Banda Neira. You have a clear view toward the town and the fort, while still feeling removed from it. The bungalows sit at the foot of the volcano and all have air conditioning and Wi-Fi. Because there are only a few units and very few guests, the place feels almost private. We received a discount for our extended stay and paid 350K with breakfast for the standard room and 400K for the deluxe bungalow. In practice the standard room is just as good, so there is little reason to take the deluxe unless you value even more privacy and your own water dispenser. The free boat shuttle to and from town is reasonably reliable and makes it very easy to go across for walks, coffee or dinner. The perfect base for staying in the Banda Islands. I would happily return, despite a few small shortcomings such as occasionally unstable Wi-Fi and coffee or tea not being freely available at all times. lava flow snorkeling ★★★★★ 15 Mar 2026 FVPR+Q4, Nusantara, Central Maluku Regency, Maluku, Indonesia Lava flow is probably the most famous snorkeling site in the Banda Islands. It lies along the coast of Banda Api and can be reached either by boat or by swimming along the reef from the nearby black sand beach. The beach itself is about a relaxed half-hour walk from Allan Bungalows through the fishing village. From there it takes roughly 45 minutes to swim out to the first Lava flow. The swim is quite strenuous, but the reef along the way is almost continuous coral with only a few rocky sections in between. Those rocky patches are often where reef sharks appear, and I saw several on the way out. There are actually two Lava flow sites close to each other. The first one has a very attractive reef with healthy hard and soft corals and a good amount of fish life. I also encountered a turtle there. The second Lava Stream, a bit further north, looks quite different. The visibility there was excellent and the reef drops off much more steeply, creating a dramatic underwater landscape. It would also be a very good place for scuba diving. Snorkelling here is special not only because of the reef but also because you are directly below Gunung Api, with the massive lava fields from past eruptions rising out of the water right next to you. One of the most impressive snorkeling spots in the Banda Islands.

PROV: Maluku / Kei Islands · 7 reviews
NAME: Forganza Resto & Cafe
ADDR: 
TEXT: ★★★★★ 21 Mar 2026 · Rp 125–150k · Dinner Kelanit, Kei Kecil, Sotheast Maluku Regency, Maluku, Indonesia Probably the best restaurant on the island, and the one we kept going back to, is Forganza Café, just outside town towards the beach area. It is certainly the biggest restaurant on the island, but deservedly popular. On our first visit it was fully booked, and we could not even get a table. They have a massive barbecue, and all the fish and seafood is grilled over coconut shells. While their sea grape ceviche is a bit too coconut-heavy for my taste, they clearly have the best grilled squid. I also really like their stir-fried leafy greens. They do add a 10% tax on top of the bill, but they charge 65K for a whole grilled squid, 15K for sea grapes, and just 8K for a lime juice, so it really does not hurt. Ten Cafe ★★★★★ 22 Mar 2026 · Rp 125–150k · Dinner 8JMM+2W8, Ngilngof, Kei Kecil, Sotheast Maluku Regency, Maluku, Indonesia Ten Café is the only proper restaurant around Ngurbloat, and that is why most tourists end up eating here. The setting is excellent, with direct views over the wide stretch of white sand. All the food is freshly prepared, so it takes a while to arrive, but it is cooked with care. I really liked the black pepper squid and prawns, as well as their version of sea grape ceviche, which you find all over the island, but this was my favourite. The grilled seafood is not quite as good as in the more local places around Langgur, and prices are roughly 30% higher. Still, for anyone staying around Ngurbloat, this is a godsend. Kei Kecil, Kabupaten Maluku Tenggara, Maluku, Indonesia Air Goa Hawang is possibly my favourite place on the island, a beautiful jungle cave with a pool of crystal-clear, cool water that is perfect for a refreshing swim, with bats flying overhead. Ww went twice and both times had the place completely to ourselves, although it might get busy at weekends. It is also remarkably clean for a tourist attraction in Indonesia. Ngur Vat Namsir Ohoi Wab ★★★★★ 22 Mar 2026 5MWP+7J6, Wab, Kei Kecil, Sotheast Maluku Regency, Maluku, Indonesia This is a gorgeous stretch of sand, slightly narrower than some of the other beaches, but still very picturesque and great for swimming. There is no accommodation here. To get here by motorbike, do not follow Google Maps navigation, the bridge is open and that way it is much closer Ngurbloat Beach ★★★★☆ 22 Mar 2026 Ngurbloat, Kabupaten Maluku Tenggara, Maluku, Indonesia Ngurbloat is the main beach on Kei Kecil and the area where most of the accommodation is located. It is a long stretch of very fine, powdery white sand with calm, clear water that is ideal for swimming. When we arrived after a period of heavy rain, the beach was in surprisingly poor condition, with large amounts of plastic washed up and hardly any recognisable sandy beach. Things changed quickly once the weather improved. With calm seas and sunshine, the beach showed up again as a wide, blindingly white stretch of sand with crystal-clear water. There are simple kiosks and picnic huts along parts of the beach, and quite a few concrete buildings built directly onto the sand in a rather odd Moorish or Mediterranean style. Both take away any romantic tropical beach feel, and overall I have quite mixed feelings about this place. Compared to the beaches further south, which feel far more natural and untouched, it also feels like tourism development here has not really been done right. The garbage problem is clearly seasonal. Some effort is made to keep the beach clean, but it depends very much on conditions. The beach only shows it's full beauty on calm, sunny days. Tanjung Vat La Roa ★★★★★ 22 Mar 2026 8JFP+Q3, Ngilngof, Sotheast Maluku Regency, Maluku, Indonesia Tanjung Vat La Roa is a worthwhile beauty spot close to Ngurbloat, a series of secluded and picturesque white sand coves that are perfect for swimming at low tide. They are connected by wooden plankways and small bridges, which give the whole place a slight Robinson Crusoe feel, even though it is just a five-minute bumpy bike ride or a leisurely 20-minute walk past Ten Café.

PROV: West Papua / Raja Ampat · 10 reviews
NAME: Blacktip Homestay
ADDR: 
TEXT: ★★★★☆ 20 Feb 2026 CMM5+26C, Yenbuba, Ransiwor, Indonesia Blacktip Homestay is all about location. Set on tiny Ransiwor Island between Kri Island and Mansuar Island, the setting is exceptional. At low tide, sandbanks appear and you can walk between the islands. It is a remarkably beautiful spot. There are just three overwater bungalows, very simple in design. Inside: a mattress with mosquito net and a small table. Outside: a terrace with a hammock. There is a fan, though the constant sea breeze usually makes it unnecessary. Electricity runs in the evenings (roughly 6 pm to midnight). At 470K rupiah per night including three meals, this is still among the cheaper options in Raja Ampat and offers very good value. The food was consistently good, often featuring well-cooked Spanish mackerel with rice, vegetables and tempeh. Portions were generous. Bathrooms are shared with the neighboring resort. They are basic but functional, with mandi-style washing and a Western toilet. The only real drawback is that the owner is not particularly welcoming or proactive. Also, our booking was initially mishandled and we had to spend the first night elsewhere. While this kind of mix-up does happen in Raja Ampat, I have to subtract one star for that. Overall, though, this is an excellent choice in an outstanding location, especially for independent travelers. Jetty soul diver (der große Steg) ★★★★★ 23 Feb 2026 CMP7+Q43 Pulau Mansuar Kecil (Kri, Yenbuba, Meos Mansar, Raja Ampat Regency, Southwest Papua, Indonesia Very easy snorkelling straight off the jetty. The coral isn’t pristine, but the fish life is outstanding. At times it genuinely feels like swimming inside an aquarium. Kordiris Dive Homestay ★★★★★ 23 Feb 2026 Pulau Gam, Raja Ampat, Yenwaoupnor, Meos Mansar, Raja Ampat Regency, Southwest Papua 98482, Indonesia Probably the place I would most happily return to in Raja Ampat. Gorgeous location on a small island off Gam, with nine bungalows, most of them built on stilts over the water. Comfort is noticeably better than some of the ultra-basic homestays elsewhere. Big beds, spacious verandas, hammocks, great views. At around 411K rupiah all inclusive, it’s probably one of the best value options in Raja Ampat. The weak point is the house reef. Parts of it are quite damaged, and snorkeling directly from the bungalow is definitely not as good as at places like Yenbuba or around Kri. You can still get lucky — on my first snorkel I saw a dugong, a whitetip shark and a lionfish within half an hour — but for consistently great snorkeling you’ll usually want to go out by boat. That’s not really a problem here. The place is very sociable, with a mixed crowd of snorkelers and divers, and it’s easy to find people to share boat costs, which matters given how expensive boats are in Raja Ampat. Diving at around 500K including equipment is among the cheapest in the area, and the gear was in decent condition. The setup is fairly laissez-faire, which I liked, though it may suit experienced divers more than complete beginners. Food was generally pretty good. Dinner and lunch were solid and tasty, though breakfast was the weakest meal — often sweet pastries and pancakes rather than something more substantial. Still, overall the food was perfectly acceptable. Not perfect, but an excellent choice overall. Manta Ridge ★★★★★ 23 Feb 2026 CGQR+67X, Arborek, Meos Mansar, Raja Ampat Regency, Papua Bar., Indonesia Snorkelled here and it was extraordinary. We saw numerous manta rays, and they came incredibly close without us chasing them or interfering in any way. It felt like a pure natural spectacle — almost as if they were performing for us, even though of course they weren’t. One of the absolute highlights of the trip. Yenbuba Jetty ★★★★★ 23 Feb 2026 CMH5+X3, Yenbuba, Raja Ampat Regency, West Papua, Indonesia For me, one of the best snorkelling spots in Raja Ampat. Go early. When there are no dive boats around, the fish life is spectacular. Huge schools of fish, big reef species, turtles, even Napoleon wrasse under the jetty. Later in the day it gets busier and noticeably less impressive. The reef stretch from here towards Kri is excellent as well. Bongso Homestay ★★★★☆ 20 Feb 2026 Pulau Kri kecil, Yenbuba, Waisai, Kabupaten Raja Ampat, Papua Barat Daya 98471, Indonesia We stayed at Bonso Homestay on Kri Island only because our original guesthouse was overbooked. Piaynemo ★★★★★ 23 Feb 2026 Groot Fam Saukabu Kepulauan, Saukabu, Waigeo Barat Kepulauan, Raja Ampat Regency, Papua Barat 98481, Indonesia Yes, it’s famous. And yes, it’s worth it. Even the approach by boat into the narrow lagoon between the limestone karst formations is beautiful — a bit like a miniature version of Ha Long Bay. Climbing up to the viewpoint gives you the classic Raja Ampat panorama, the one that appears on the 100,000 rupiah note. It’s an expensive trip by boat, and I still think boat prices in Raja Ampat are generally inflated. But as a landscape experience, this is something you shouldn’t skip. We were lucky to arrive late and had the viewpoint almost to ourselves, which made it even better. Rufas Island ★★★★★ 15 Mar 2026 C7PM+4QG, Saukabu, Waigeo Barat Kepulauan, Raja Ampat Regency, Southwest Papua, Indonesia Rufas Island was one of the snorkeling stops on the way to Piaynemo. The underwater landscape here is quite unusual, with large overhanging rocks and a small arch that you can swim through into a sheltered lagoon that almost feels like a natural aquarium. The reef is in good condition and there is a lot of fish life. I saw plenty of reef fish and several reef sharks while snorkeling here. A beautiful and very scenic snorkeling stop if you are exploring the Piaynemo area by boat.

Why not Goa / North Goa / Assagao · 2 reviews G-Shot Coffee Roastery & Cafe H. No 436, Socol Vaddo, Assagao, Goa 403507, India The pretty village of Assagao is where you'll find hands down the best espresso drinks in Goa. Coffee culture in India has made a quantum leap in the last decade, but finding a truly perfect cup of flat white or cappuccino is still an absolute rarity, even in the hipster cafés of the biggest cities. G-shot, in a nice tranquil garden setting, does brew and prepare coffees of a quality and texture you'd expect in the best cafés of Melbourne or Berlin. They also charge prices similar to those in aforementioned cities, making this by far the most expensive cup of coffee I had in all of India. It was around 250 Rs. They also have some rather pricey vegan hipster food which isn't my cup of tea. But for the best coffees, it's definitely worth the trip Vinayak Family Restaurant House No 278, Socol Vaddo, Assagao, Goa 403507, India In beautiful, peaceful Assagao, next to a rice paddy, this busy popular family restaurant specialises in Goan seafood. The sauces are so creamy, the soups so oily, it's almost indecent.
